On Tue, 31 Oct 2006, tonyr wrote:

> I am not Slackware conversant, but the little bit of reading that I did
> leads me to believe that there are two paths to keymap modification. One
> is at startup, through the *rc* process, either via /*etc/rc.d/rc.keymap*
> or *rc.local*, using *loadkeys* to read a keymap file in a known location.
> In this case *loadkeys *would indeed be running as *root, *and so would
> succeed.

Tony,

   Yes, I have been changing the ctrl and cap lock keys for many years now by
using loadkeys and ~/.keymap. It works well on other systems, but there must
be something with the notebook that's getting in the way. For reference, all
systems run the same distribution release and kernel.

> The other way is through an X session startup, in which case the keymap
> modifications should be in *~/.Xmodmap*, who's format, I believe, is not
> the same as a keymap file read by *loadkeys*.

   X is different, as you note. It reads ~/.Xmodmap and that works flawlessly
in the same machine that's decided to be recalcitrant at the console.

> None of my searching turned up an example where a local user's
> *~/.keymap* (or ~/.<anyfoo> for that matter) was used, in Slackware
> or anywhere else. I'm gonna guess that you've been using the
> ~/.keymap method for a relatively long time, and maybe even have
> a *loadkeys* command in your .login or .profile or .bashrc or .cshrc
> or whatever your shell startup file is.

   It's in ~/.bash_profile so it's always running -- when it works, that is
-- in each console.

   I'll figure out a kludge if I can't fix the problem.

Thanks,

Rich

it. When I get home I have to change back. I created profiles for PSU
and home, the home one works within 30 seconds or so, but the PSU one
doesn't work at all. I have to do it manually there by clicking through
all the above.

The kdialog line above is cool. (Learning new stuff here.) First, I
installed ifscheme with Synaptic, then tried the command. It popped up

# from John Jason Jordan
# on Wednesday 01 November 2006 07:28 am:

>So I guess I need to create the database that the combobox is looking
>for. 

No.

kdialog only prints what you selected on stdout.

ifswitch uses it to ask what you want and then juggle your network,

But you need to have /etc/network/interfaces in order before it will do 
you any good.

This is not a configuration tool, only a switcher.  If you've been using 
a gui config tool, I guess you'll have to hope it speaks ifupdown.

Read the earlier e-mail.

--Eric

Message-ID: <1162402260.11318.36.camel@sparrow>

Have you all looked at networkmanager? If you use gnome it works pretty
well. Its included in the Automatix kit for Ubuntu now. It uses dbus so
you have to wipe your /etc/network/interfaces clean. In the past it was
dependent on dhcp but I think you can set static profiles now(not sure
about that though).
jm

I googled *loadkeys permission* and a lot of stuff turned up. 
There seems to have been some sort of hiccup in the kernel
sometime in the  2.4.31 - 2.4.33 timeframe.  The suggestion
that turned up a couple of times was to update the *kbd
*package (whatever that means for Slackware).

- tony

thats your issue

      home to a number of major Open Source projects.  The

      are also neat and provide ways of getting undergraduates 
      involved with OpenSource software.

      little demo of the One Laptop Per Child dev motherboard that he has.

If you are using Cygwin / XWin, then you may want to use the following
command:

    Local$ xhost +remotehost
    Local$ ssh -Y user at remotehost
    RemoteHost$ konqueror &

and then bring the application forward to your desktop to display it in
your local XWin.

If you need more info, you can email the list or me directly as I use this
technique regularly at work.

Tim

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Wed Nov  1 23:11:29 2006
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Wed, 1 Nov 2006 23:11:29 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Firefox 2.0 Install - too difficult?
Message-ID: <20061102071129.GA20651@gate.kl-ic.com>


Tonight I was helping a friend learn about Linux - we got through a
lot (where and what to search on Google, upgrading, rpms, etc.).  

One rough spot was when we attempted to upgrade Firefox 1.5.0.7 to
Firefox 2.0 .  We figured out how, but the process was painful;
there is no online documentation for upgrading 1.5 to 2.0 that
describes what to do and where things go.  This was upgrading a
SUSE 10 system, so we decided not to do a real install.  We will
wait for SUSE to provide an RPM that puts everything in the right
places for SUSE. 

 was unpleasantly surprised at how undocumented and newbie-unfriendly
the manual tar and move links and find plugins process was.  I would
not expect an unaided newbie to try this.  This is of course
compounded by the problem that a browser is a critical item to
re-install;  if you goof up, it will be difficult to go back out on
the web seeking help.

Am I expecting too little from newbies, or expecting too much
too quickly from the firefox people?  Again, I expect SUSE 10
will have a Firefox 2.0 RPM upgrade in a week or two, but most 
newbies won't have such an easy time of it.

Keith

-- 
Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993
KLIC --- Keith Lofstrom Integrated Circuits --- "Your Ideas in Silicon"
Design Contracting in Bipolar and CMOS - Analog, Digital, and Scan ICs

From pmvw at outwardfocus.net  Thu Nov  2 01:20:29 2006
From: pmvw at outwardfocus.net (Piet van Weel)

In-Reply-To: <20061102071129.GA20651@gate.kl-ic.com>

Well Keith...

Honestly I'll be surprised if SUSE will have firefox 2.0 very quickly. One
of the things that makes *in some aspects* SUSE harder, is the factor that
it is really challenging doing a source upgrade. This is due to the large
amount of customizations which occur. (It's like Real Estate, location,
location, location.)

The advantage is that if you're using YAST and SUSE has released it, it's
generally pretty good at working from the get go. (There have been times
when it wasn't that way.) The downside is that you're not usually going to
get the latest and greatest, but it will be very stable.

Piet

You may wish to try out the Firefox 2.0
packages available in the openSUSE buildservice:
http://software.opensuse.org/download/repositories/mozilla/SUSE_Linux_10.0/

(I *think* but don't know for sure that you can add that URL as an
installation source in 10.0's yast and then be able pull in any necessary
dependencies automatically.)

You can read more about the openSUSE build service at
http://en.opensuse.org/Build_Service/User . The people maintaining the
Mozilla packages are both people from SUSE (unfortunately, the build
service requires an account to see who's maintaining a specific project).

From rshepard at appl-ecosys.com  Thu Nov  2 05:59:57 2006
From: rshepard at appl-ecosys.com (Rich Shepard)
Date: Thu, 2 Nov 2006 05:59:57 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Re: [Insert name here] Install - too difficult?
In-Reply-To: <200611012340.40928.guy1656@opusnet.com>
References: <200611012311829.SM11192@mx02-oc.opusnet.com>
	<200611012340.40928.guy1656@opusnet.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0611020554240.8425@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>

On Thu, 2 Nov 2006, GLL wrote:

> I downloaded the .gz, .tz or whatever file but I haven't installed it yet
> - I would have to pore through my Linux books to find that note where I
> wrote down what do do with a stupid "not a normal ZIP and doesn't install
> with a double-click" file...

   1.) mv <file> to desired directory and run 'tar xzvf <filename.gz/.tgz>'
   2.) cd to the created directory, filename/
   3.) check configuration options ('./configure | less'), then run
'./configure'
   4.) make
   5.) make install (or checkinstall if you want a Slackware, Red Hat, or
Debian package)

> One thing I like about Linux is that it runs for years without maintenance
> or upgrades... I've even forgotten what the hell I'm running, and there's
> nothing in the 'Star' menu that even says what this system is...

   Er, better do the security upgrades for your distribution as soon as they
come out. If you're not on the security mail list, find it and subscribe.

Rich

It picked up my old settings just fine, it should store everything in
<home> regardless of where you run it from.  Plugins installed under
the installation dir. will need to move if you move the binary, of
course, but you can put them in your home dir anyway.

> Keith is right, it should be easier (another
> plug for Ubuntu here).

This is one of the biggest problems with deployment on linux....
possibly the biggest problem with linux.  There are *so many*
variations of linux, each with a slightly different file system, or
slightly different libraries in slightly different places.... you
either have to know how to do it your self, or you have to wait.  It's
not reasonable to expect a project maintainer to cater to everyone's
needs -- that's precisely why we have distributions.

Firefox *is* easy to install, compared to many things.  Pick an app at
random and try installing it w/out using a distro package.   Say, Open
Office ;)

--Rogan

From ed at alcpress.com  Thu Nov  2 15:36:40 2006
From: ed at alcpress.com (Ed Sawicki)
Date: Thu, 02 Nov 2006 15:36:40 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Pigs flying II
Message-ID: <454A8108.6050209@alcpress.com>

I just viewed the joint Microsoft/Novell announcement.
The core of the announcement is that Novell has agreed
to compensate Microsoft for its Intellectual Property.
When customers buy Novell SuSE Linux, they pay an
"upfront balancing payment" that earns them a patent
covenant from Microsoft.

Steve Balmer made it clear that if you buy or use
something other than Novell SuSE Linux, you will have
no such covenant and will be at risk.

I'm wondering how this is different that the license
fee SCO offered for Linux users. This announcement seems
to guarantee Microsoft a revenue stream from Linux sales.

Microsoft promised not to bring action against Open Source
developers - all developers apparently - not just those
who develop for SuSE Linux.

They also announced technical cooperation on things
like virtualization technologies, interoperability,
and document formats (Office/OpenOffice interoperability).

Ed Sawicki

http://arstechnica.com/news.ars/post/20061102-8141.html
------------------------------
Strange bedfellows: Microsoft, Novell ink pact

11/2/2006 3:28:11 PM, by Eric Bangeman

At a press conference in San Francisco, Microsoft CEO Steve Ballmer
and Novell CEO Ronald Hovsepian announced a new partnership between
Microsoft and Novell. The unprecedented deal will have Microsoft
offering a degree of sales support for Novell's SUSE Linux while
both companies work towards better interoperability between their
respective operating systems. As part of the agreement, Microsoft
also promises not to wield its patent portfolio against SUSE Linux.
(more in article)

From plug_0 at robinson-west.com  Thu Nov  2 16:20:48 2006
From: plug_0 at robinson-west.com (Unknown)

Subject: [PLUG] USB-P1K phone poorly suppoted.

I bought it off of http://www.von-phone.com/ because it was advertised
as being Linux compatible.  It barely is.  The darn thing requires
Fedora Core 3 and even then you can't use the keypad on it.

$30 is more than a TracFone and a TracFone not only works, it sounds
better than this thing does.

http://www.von-phone.com/support.php links to the support page for this
product.

I give this product a 1/5 rating.  Big tip, it uses the OSS sound
drivers and doesn't work with Alsa.

I am as dissatisfied with this product as I was with the Intel 536EP
chipset modem that I couldn't use the voice features of under Linux.

Why do companies say works with Linux on their web sites but drop that
little note on their product cds?  Worse, why is the support inferior?
This USB device doesn't look that complicated.  Someone else could
probably do it better.

Michael C. Robinson



From plug_0 at robinson-west.com  Thu Nov  2 18:51:32 2006
From: plug_0 at robinson-west.com (Unknown)
Date: Thu, 02 Nov 2006 18:51:32 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Microsoft and SuSE/Novell sign agreement
In-Reply-To: <20061103010334.GB32203@gate.kl-ic.com>

On Thu, 2006-11-02 at 17:03 -0800, Keith Lofstrom wrote:
> Wow ... and ... Wow.   Time to plan that ski vacation in hell...
> 
> 
> http://arstechnica.com/news.ars/post/20061102-8141.html
> ------------------------------
> Strange bedfellows: Microsoft, Novell ink pact
> 
> 11/2/2006 3:28:11 PM, by Eric Bangeman
> 
> At a press conference in San Francisco, Microsoft CEO Steve Ballmer
> and Novell CEO Ronald Hovsepian announced a new partnership between
> Microsoft and Novell. The unprecedented deal will have Microsoft
> offering a degree of sales support for Novell's SUSE Linux while
> both companies work towards better interoperability between their
> respective operating systems. As part of the agreement, Microsoft
> also promises not to wield its patent portfolio against SUSE Linux.
> (more in article)
> 
> Keith
> 

Would this be a good time to point out that Steve Gibson's review of
Vmware and Microsoft's offering favored VMware hands down?  Apparently,
Microsoft doesn't know jack about doing virtualized machines.  Every 
version of Windows, from what I can tell, has been designed to break
program compatibility.  Why support running Windows NT in a virtual
environment if you can make more money forcing companies to upgrade
to Microsoft Server 2003?

As far as the Redhat should be worried comment in the mentioned article,
why?  Redhat is in a different market than Microsoft is.  Microsoft has
no grounds to threaten Linux users with patent infringement lawsuits.
The purpose of patents is to increase public access to and fair use of
technology.  Attempting to use the patent system to create an empire is
an abuse of it and shows a lack of consideration.

For a while, I've been hoping that ReactOS will become more functional
for deskop use.  I think it would be better to prove to Microsoft and
the world that you don't need Windows, or any Windows compatible system,
to accomplish fantastic computing feats.  

Windows is not a good operating system.  Microsoft basically ignores the
Internet Engineering Task Force's every recommendation.  The registry
concept of Windows has become a monstrosity as various software vendors
and even Microsoft itself have abused it.  If the courts would get their
act together, Microsoft would be in trouble for threatening to sue Linux
users without grounds to do so.  

Isn't harassment against the law no matter how rich and powerful you
think you are?  Isn't it slanderous to lie about patent infringement
from a competitor when there isn't any infringement?  Does this strike
anyone, lying about patent infringement, as anticompetitive?

I think the response to this partnership is to generate more demand for
Linux.  If Microsoft is crazy enough to try and sue Linux users, I hope
people rise up and put Steve Ballmer in his place.  By rising up I'm
advocating: Microsoft software boycotts, helping people use alternative
software, and helping further the development of open source software
solutions.

Michael C. Robinson

You can bypass Windows lack of support for large fat32 volumes by using
something like partition magic to create the partitions, I caution I haven't
done this in a few years but _did_ actually work .. I created the max
partition size allowed by windows to start then used PM to non-destructively
increase the size past the limit. NTFS should be avoided at all costs (if
you value your data) IMHO atleast for the time being.


Drew-

From ehem at m5p.com  Fri Nov  3 16:51:25 2006
From: ehem at m5p.com (Elliott Mitchell)
Date: Fri, 3 Nov 2006 16:51:25 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] NTFS Support?
In-Reply-To: <20061104003756.3FC3347DA@ulke.nakedape.cc>
Message-ID: <200611040051.kA40pPkx006968@m5p.com>

>From: Jason Van Cleve <jvancleve at chrome.com>
> Can anyone offer advice on the state and stability of NTFS support.  I just
> bought a 300 gig' HD for backups, and apparently that's too large for FAT32.
> I have Gentoo with kernel 2.6.oh.hell.i.dont.know.offhand on my laptop, and
> I'd like to use the drive with that as well as with WinXP.  Is linux NTFS
> support solid, or should I use EXT3 or reiser?

FAT is just a wee bit nasty so I'd tend to avoid that if possible. I'm
not entirely sure of its stability, but I'd point towards UDF. Apparently
the less privledged system does support full read-write on UDF, and I've
seen it stated that UDF tends to be used on the larger USB keys (for
which sparing sectors are important, unlike hard drives). I do know it is
possible for Linux to mount and write UDF filesystems, just I'm not
entirely sure of the stability. `fsck.udf` would be good to keep handy.

From scratchcomputing at gmail.com  Fri Nov  3 19:05:57 2006
From: scratchcomputing at gmail.com (Eric Wilhelm)
Date: Fri, 3 Nov 2006 19:05:57 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Microsoft and SuSE/Novell sign agreement
In-Reply-To: <20061103010334.GB32203@gate.kl-ic.com>
References: <20061103010334.GB32203@gate.kl-ic.com>
Message-ID: <200611031905.57367.ewilhelm@cpan.org>

# from Keith Lofstrom
# on Thursday 02 November 2006 05:03 pm:

>Wow ... and ... Wow. ? Time to plan that ski vacation in hell...

Better plan it for a few years out.  And even then, get refundable 
tickets.

There's nothing new here.  Having watched the press conference, I'm 
mostly hearing that MS feels entitled to extract licensing fees from 
Linux users (likely by virtue of their patent on the backslash and 
similar "innovations".)

What puzzles me is how this doesn't put Novell on the wrong side of the 
GPL.  It implies that only licensed SUSE customers are granted a 
license to use this supposed MS IP.  If this is the case, I would 
assume that this license is not universally transferable, which sounds 
like the imposition of restrictions on GPL'd code not owned by Novell 
-- hence voiding their right to use said code.  Guess we'll see what 
the courts think about this having-and-eating-not-your-cake business.

The other fun fact is their claim that they'll grant a covenant to 
"individual" open-source developers.  That means as long as you're 
writing free software and not running a company, they will be happy to 
steal your work and not sue you as soon as they file a patent for it.  
If you have money to extract, I guess that's a different story.

--Eric

"Everything should be made as simple as possible, but no simpler."
--Albert Einstein

I have not used every distro, but I've seen a few, and I've never seen
anything as wonky as yast.

If a distro migration decision is to be based upon the updater utility,
then perhaps it is time to rethink the entire problem.  RPM is
inherently inferior to apt.  Some good reasons for making this claim can
be found here:

http://chris.quietlife.net/?p=152

synaptic is the GUI for performing update/install operations on a debian
machine.

Carlos Konstanski

Your "true community" options -- little or no "corporate structure" are
Debian (apt-based administration) and Gentoo (Portage-based
administration). The choice between Debian and Gentoo depends largely on
whether you want to recompile almost everything (Gentoo) or run a pure
binary (Debian) Linux.

I run Gentoo and am both locked in and happy about it. :) But it will
never win any popularity contests as long as there's Ubuntu and Fedora.

> Your "true community" options -- little or no "corporate structure" are
> Debian (apt-based administration) and Gentoo (Portage-based
> administration). The choice between Debian and Gentoo depends largely on
> whether you want to recompile almost everything (Gentoo) or run a pure
> binary (Debian) Linux.
>
> I run Gentoo and am both locked in and happy about it. :) But it will
> never win any popularity contests as long as there's Ubuntu and Fedora.

I'm totally with you.  suse to gentoo is a big leap, though.  I went
from redhat 8 to knoppix 3.4 to pure debian to gentoo, a process that took
2 years.  Once I hit gentoo, I have been a happy camper for 2 years
more and counting.

Regarding ubuntu and fedora: at my job, where I have been working for
the past year, I have watched as former linux naysayers are (through my
efforts) been coming around.  There's a guy who has been fighting with
fedora for a month or two.  He put ubuntu on his home machine, and likes
it way better.  I'm all for it.  If there's a debian distro that
everyone likes better than the redhat family of distros, and if ubuntu
can get more widely supported among the big corporate vendors (hardware
ones especially), we may start seeing debian make its way into Houses of
Microsoft like the one I work at.  That can do only good for us staunch
linux users who have to work in these environments.  I get to run gentoo
on my workstation, but I am the only one in an 800-employee company who
has this privilege.  I pay for it by being the java dev.

Gentoo users should remember to be thankful for all the debian community
has given us: common-lisp-controller, and the new and improved java setup,
come to mind.

Carlos Konstanski

From znmeb at cesmail.net  Sat Nov  4 15:40:29 2006
From: znmeb at cesmail.net (M. Edward (Ed) Borasky)
Date: Sat, 04 Nov 2006 15:40:29 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Linux distro recommendation as a replacement for SuSE
In-Reply-To: <200611041247.31287.alex@daniloff.com>
References: <200611040914.55603.alex@daniloff.com>	<41704.10.0.1.188.1162670286.squirrel@petelancashire.com>
	<200611041247.31287.alex@daniloff.com>
Message-ID: <454D24ED.4050801@cesmail.net>

Alex Daniloff wrote:
> I'm going to use it mostly to deploy my applications and web based services to 
> my customers. That is why I'm trying to avoid any potential claims and 
> mitigations from M$-Novell hunchos against my business.
> 
> Alex

A word or two of advice:

1. If your concern is avoiding lawsuits, hire an attorney and take his
or her advice. This isn't a technical matter, after all -- it's the
legal health of your business that's at stake.

2. If you want to be compatible with the 900-pound gorillas in the Linux
business -- for example, if you want to hire certified systems
administrators, etc. -- your choice of distro really boils down to three
options.

   a. Red Hat Enterprise. If you can afford it, it's stable, well
supported and the horse to beat.

   b. Fedora. There's a very strong community and all the support Red
Hat can *legally* provide.

   c. Novell SuSE Enterprise.

I'd recommend staying away from CentOS. I've used it, and I haven't had
any problems whatsoever with it, and it seems to be what it claims to be
-- a community-driven rebuild of Red Hat Enterprise Linux. My hesitation
to recommend it is based on concerns about the strength of the community
relative to the strength of the Fedora community. CentOS is *competing*
with Red Hat and Fedora is *co-operating* with Red Hat. That's a *big*
difference!

And I'd recommend staying away from both Gentoo and the Debian-based
distros -- Ubuntu and Debian itself. The communities are strong, and the
package management and system administration tools are first rate. But
they are *different* from Red Hat -- the 900-pound gorilla. That's a
cost to you, the business owner.

On Sat, 2006-11-04 at 15:40 -0800, M. Edward (Ed) Borasky wrote:

> I'd recommend staying away from CentOS. I've used it, and I haven't had
> any problems whatsoever with it, and it seems to be what it claims to be
> -- a community-driven rebuild of Red Hat Enterprise Linux. My hesitation
> to recommend it is based on concerns about the strength of the community
> relative to the strength of the Fedora community. CentOS is *competing*
> with Red Hat and Fedora is *co-operating* with Red Hat. That's a *big*
> difference!

I disagree.  Regardless of the relationship between CentOS and RHEL,
CentOS is a very strong choice--it has the stability and familiarity of
RHEL without the price tag (which honestly isn't that bad at $300/yr).
If you want to get, say, your RHCE you can learn it on CentOS.

The additional benefit is that RHEL remains an easy option--if you have
customers who want to pay for support or want to run a proprietary
application on a certified platform in production, you can use RHEL and
use CentOS for dev and QA.

If you have a customer with a RHEL server which they no longer want to
pay for support, you can just switch update sources to CentOS and not
worry about it.

If you maintain a collection of locally-built packages, you need only
build them once (per major version).

Fedora isn't a good choice for commercial uses like this because its
lifespan is frightfully short and fedora-legacy near death.  I like it
on my own workstations because I always want the latest there, but my
servers are all CentOS.

Wil

From znmeb at cesmail.net  Sat Nov  4 17:08:51 2006
From: znmeb at cesmail.net (M. Edward (Ed) Borasky)
Date: Sat, 04 Nov 2006 17:08:51 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] USB hard drives and Linux
In-Reply-To: <200611041648.44365.carla@bratgrrl.com>
References: <200611041648.44365.carla@bratgrrl.com>
Message-ID: <454D39A3.2060101@cesmail.net>

Carla Schroder wrote:
> I want to buy an external USB hard drive to use for quick backups on my Linux 
> boxens- are there any Linux gotchas with these? Can I buy one without 
> worrying if it's going to work on Linux?
> 
Pretty much all USB drives work with Linux. However, some of the more
clever vendors have gone out of their way to be Linux compatible. Check
the boxes at CompUSA and Fry's, and search the web.

As to gotchas, if you're counting on using software supplied with the
drive, it probably won't work on Linux. And one big gotcha is that a USB
drive is usually formatted FAT32. If you hope to share it with other
operating systems, you won't want to re-format it. And if you need to
re-format it, you're better off doing that on a Windows system. Windows
puts some extra things on when it formats a partition.

If you plan to use it for Linux only, you're free to reformat it with
something that has Linux-specific features, of course. Big external USB
drives tend to be slower than internal hard drives, so you might want to
choose a filesystem that's optimized for a lot of writing of the type of
files you're planning to back up.

I bought a "Fantom" 250GB external USB 2.0 drive to and my laptop, running 
Linux, detected it when I plugged it in. The entire drive came formatted from 
the factory as NTFS and so I shrunk the partition size down and created a 2nd 
partition and made an "ext3" filesystem. 

Unfortunately I need to dual-boot my laptop so I need to backup data for both 
WinXP and Linux from my laptop. IIRC I was running SuSE 9.2 at the time I 
made the original drive purchase and it worked flawlessly. I would guess that 
any reasonable Linux distro with good USB support would work as flawlessly as 
SuSE' Linux in terms of supporing a USB 2.0 drive.

I use amd-64 version of Ubuntu Dapper and it works great in all
respects except a couple of things, one of which is flash. Other
plugins are sometimes a bitch too. If I really needed flash and
multimedia plugins working in my browsers I would just install the
32-bit versions of the browsers. Right now I use Crossover Office
(getting WINE working on 64-bit is doable, but a lot of hassle), and
Crossover Office has a list of supported programs that you can just
click and install. One of them was Quicktime, so I installed it. It
installed itself as a plugin in Opera, but I can't figure out how to
get it working in Firefox. 

You can go to the Ubuntu 64-bit forum and find a lot of advice on
getting stuff working on 64-bit Ubuntu. Most of the advice is
appropriate for other 64-bit distros as well. Look for posts by a guy
who uses the nick Killz; he seems to have a pretty good handle on this
stuff. He advocates the 32-bit browsers and has instructions/scripts
for installing them on 64-bit Ubuntu without using a 32-bit chroot
environment.

I haven't tried getting those things working in 64-bit Edgy yet,
because I'm not going to install it until a month from now when finals
are over. I've booted the live CD, and I noted that Firefox did not
seem to have any flash or multimedia capability. So evidently those
things are not going to get installed by default.

On Sat, 4 Nov 2006 16:48:44 -0800
Carla Schroder <carla at bratgrrl.com> dijo:

> I want to buy an external USB hard drive to use for quick backups on my Linux

First, you made another sale of your book the other day. A copy now
resides in the bookshelf behind me. :)

As for USB drives, as others have noted, they "just work." At least on
my Ubuntu Dapper amd-64 machine they do. I plug one in and Nautilus
pops up a browser window. All I had to do was create a mount point
"/media/usbdisk" and mounting is a snap. Both of mine are formatted
ext3, the same as the hard disk partitions on my computer. 

But having said that, I have some problems that make me wonder. For
example, if I use Kdar to make a backup, half the time the computer
locks up solid -- no keyboard, no mouse -- in the middle of a backup.
It seems to happen mostly when Kdar is chewing on a large file. A
couple of times I have had lockups just copying large files to and from
the USB disk, i.e., with Nautilus. Is there a problem with the USB
driver? I can't say. I know I have googled and never found any major
complaints. If my problems were caused by a bug in the USB driver you'd
think there would be serious screaming all over the Linux forums. So do
I just have flaky drives? One is the original drive that came with this
computer. The other is a Pocketec sold specifically for backing up
laptops. And I can also add that my USB ports work flawlessly otherwise
-- my mouse has never failed me, for example.

It's all a mystery to me. All I know is that I don't trust backing up
to my USB drives. Before I do I make sure I have saved all open files
and closed all programs other than what I'm using to back up the data.
If it's going to lock up at least I'm ready for it.

What I really crave is a hard drive I can stick on my home ethernet
network. They're kind of expensive, though.

This becomes an even more interesting discussion in light of the bruhaha
around Oracle Linux, which is also a "rebuild" like CentOS. As the
CentOS developers freely admit, the tools they use to rebuild aren't the
same as the tools used by Red Hat, and this may affect compatibility /
certifiability - in terms of support for specialized software (not any
LPI/RHCE sort of tests).

But this drifts away from the topic. Remember, most all of SUSE is GPL,
and built from the same source code as Red Hat, CentOS, Debian, etc. So
if Microsoft has agreed to not sue Novell, then they have no basis for
sueing Red Hat, etc. over the same code.

But then again, IANAL.

From ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com  Sun Nov  5 11:54:43 2006
From: ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com (Carlos Konstanski)
Date: Sun, 5 Nov 2006 12:54:43 -0700 (MST)
Subject: [PLUG] AMD64, Java, and Flash.
In-Reply-To: <20061105185832.GC24323@syrinxpc.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.61.0611041849260.2130@shaft.bitmine.net>
	<20061105185832.GC24323@syrinxpc.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0611051159200.12285@sphinktoo.pippiandcarlos.com>

> All signs point to 'yes'.  Why's everyone gotta run a 64-bit distro on
> their under-2GB-RAM desktops, anyway?
>
> furrfu,
>  Aaron

Perhaps the reason is because linux is all about choice.  "Because I
can" is a valid reason to run any version of linux on anything, any time.

I'm running java and flash on an amd64, and it works great.  I do employ
32-bit binary builds of java, flash and firefox, but that's only because
Sun and Adobe haven't stepped up with x86_64 builds of their products
yet.  So for me to say that java and flash work great on my amd64 is
analagous to saying that 32-bit emulation in a 64-bit OS works great on
an amd64.  If java and flash are going to run as 32-bit binaries anyway,
why limit yourself on the other 99.99% of your distro?

A year ago, it was hard to get packages like PHP, ruby and mozilla to
work well on amd64.  These issues, and may others, have long since been
resolved.  The only laggards left are the proprietary software vendors
and OpenOffice.  The day when all packages have a 64-bit build will come
sooner if more amd64 boards get sold.  Those who choose early adoption
will have a few minor struggles, but we'll manage.  Those who choose to
wait will have 32-bit boxes that run swell.  There's room in the linux
world for both camps.  Choice is our great weapon against proprietary
software.  Let us support one another in making choices.  We have enough
people trying to limit our options.

Back to the actual topic of this thread: which netinst disk to use?
Both will work for java and flash development, though the 32-bit one
will take less effort to get working than the 64-bit one.  The choice is
entirely yours, lucky fellow.

Carlos Konstanski

>
> I just realized that I don't have any real speed information on the
> various possibilities. My home wiring is CAT-6, but I don't know how it

> gigE device I have is my Linux laptop. Everything else, including my
> Windows desktop (five years old) is fast ethernet only. If I bought an
> NAS drive that had gigE connection, I wonder how fast the laptop and it
> would talk to each other. I'm talking real world v. theoretical. I
> googled and didn't find much. And what would be the comparison if I got
> a 1394b drive? That is, assuming that the Firewire port on this laptop
> is 1394b and is actually working under Dapper amd-64 -- I don't have
> any Firewire devices to test it with. I just assumed that the fastest
> solution (from a practical standpoint) would be a gigE NAS drive, but
> that may have been an unwarranted assumption.

I don't know anything about Firewire on Linux-- USB 2.0 has a theoretical 
upper limit of 480 megabits per second, and SATA 3.0 3 gigabits per second. 
Real-world speeds are less, of course, because of Ethernet and TCP/IP 
overhead, and every piece of hardware that your bits must traverse bogs them 
down a bit. Common bottlenecks are PCI buses, because they use shared 
bandwidth, and old slow hard drives. To get the best gig-e speeds, you'll 
want nice modern everything, like PCI-e, fast hard drives and NICs, hotrod 
CPUs, and of course suitable cabling and network interfaces.

On modern PCs if all you do is use gig-e NICs, switches, and cabling, you 
should get double what you were getting with fast Ethernet.

These two links have useful information:

http://www.directron.com/expressguide.html
http://www.enterprisenetworkingplanet.com/nethub/article.php/3578336

--

Thanks to you and Bill. It worked. Sort of. That is, OOo didn't puke it
up. However, it didn't change the way the data is displayed in the
form. The entries are still random, and I can't figure out why. The
order in which the entries appear in the form control is not the order
in which I entered them in the database originally, not the way the
database is currently sorted, or any other way that makes any sense. I
am assuming that the sort utilities in OOo Base are really just sorting
the display; the data remains on disk in some original order. But I may
be wrong about that. I only conclude that because that's the way other
databases I have used in the past worked, plus when I have done sorts
on this database the hard disk light never came on. But who knows.

This entire form project is turning into a major PITA. It's an
experiment to see if I can create an editable PDF file with drop-down
selection boxes that students can choose an answer from. Adobe Reader
7.0 will allow the user to edit such a file and then print it out. I
have successfully exported the form to PDF from OOo and Adobe Reader
does allow edits. But I can't get the controls to display the choices
in the order I want. Also, OOo embeds the font I'm using in the
document, but not for the controls. Evidently it's not embedding any
font at all for the controls, because when Adobe Reader opens the PDF
it is substituting one of its default fonts for the font in the
controls. And the Adobe font is not IPA capable, so half the characters
are not showing up. And finally, for some reason when I change the
value in one control in the PDF document, it suddenly makes all similar
controls display the same entry. It's like they are linked somehow. I
can't figure out how they got that way or how to unlink them.

Trying to figure out which of the zillions of options in the Propery
window for the controls needs to be changed in order to solve these
problems is driving me nuts.

counts--gcc, binutils--are the same versions.  I'm sure Red Hat a
considerable amount of infrastructure that goes into automating the
building and testing which CentOS doesn't have (or has different).  At
any rate, at my previous job we did a lot of work with Oracle and
WebLogic (and lots of other Java crap) running on CentOS and RHEL and
found no appreciable differences.  (Well, the differences were I didn't
have to wait for management to order my entitlements for CentOS before I
could do on-line post-installation.  These days, of course, I've
discovered that Yam can be used even to mirror from RHN, which I wish
I'd had or known about then.)

From randy at voshell.net  Sun Nov  5 18:43:18 2006
From: randy at voshell.net (Randy Voshell)
Date: Sun, 05 Nov 2006 18:43:18 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Re: PLUG Digest, Vol 26, Issue 8
Message-ID: <454E30C6020000B600000352@static-71-117-128-146.ptldor.dsl-w.verizon.net.>

Busy week... I haven't studied the whole announcement, so I'm probably going to end up looking extremely foolish.  Oh, well, here goes...

I think you're all a little off base with what all of this means.  In the context of virtual machines, Novell is extremely interested in Xen.  Xen is most competative in para-virtualization mode, otherwise I really have to go with VMware.  

Para-virtualization requires that the guest OS is "aware" of the host OS, knows that it is running in a virtual session, and can adapt to load conditions under control of the host OS and the hypervisor.

Novell has said that Xen is market ready for shops that wish to implement NetWare/OES and SLES-10 guest OS's.  <aside>probably not as ready for Linux/OES since it remains at SLES-9 until 2nd half 2007).  Novell says specifically that proprietary closed-source OS's such as Windows wouldn't work well in a Xen environment because it cannot be adapted without the cooperation of Microsoft.

The announcement seems to be suggesting that Microsoft is willing to cooperate -- as long as their cooperation doesn't drag Windows into the GPL.

I know I should wait until I know something before I stick my virtual foot in my actual mouth, but perhaps someone on this list with knowledge of Xen could look at Novell and Microsoft's announcement through that "filter" and see if I'm crazy.

Okay... I'm crazy, regardless.

I bought it off of http://www.von-phone.com/ because it was advertised
as being Linux compatible.  It barely is.  The darn thing requires
Fedora Core 3 and even then you can't use the keypad on it.

$30 is more than a TracFone and a TracFone not only works, it sounds
better than this thing does.

http://www.von-phone.com/support.php links to the support page for this
product.

I give this product a 1/5 rating.  Big tip, it uses the OSS sound
drivers and doesn't work with Alsa.

I am as dissatisfied with this product as I was with the Intel 536EP
chipset modem that I couldn't use the voice features of under Linux.

Why do companies say works with Linux on their web sites but drop that
little note on their product cds?  Worse, why is the support inferior?
This USB device doesn't look that complicated.  Someone else could
probably do it better.

Michael C. Robinson

On Thu, 2006-11-02 at 17:03 -0800, Keith Lofstrom wrote:
> Wow ... and ... Wow.   Time to plan that ski vacation in hell...
> 
> 
> http://arstechnica.com/news.ars/post/20061102-8141.html
> ------------------------------
> Strange bedfellows: Microsoft, Novell ink pact
> 
> 11/2/2006 3:28:11 PM, by Eric Bangeman
> 
> At a press conference in San Francisco, Microsoft CEO Steve Ballmer
> and Novell CEO Ronald Hovsepian announced a new partnership between
> Microsoft and Novell. The unprecedented deal will have Microsoft
> offering a degree of sales support for Novell's SUSE Linux while
> both companies work towards better interoperability between their
> respective operating systems. As part of the agreement, Microsoft
> also promises not to wield its patent portfolio against SUSE Linux.
> (more in article)
> 
> Keith
> 

Would this be a good time to point out that Steve Gibson's review of
Vmware and Microsoft's offering favored VMware hands down?  Apparently,
Microsoft doesn't know jack about doing virtualized machines.  Every 
version of Windows, from what I can tell, has been designed to break
program compatibility.  Why support running Windows NT in a virtual
environment if you can make more money forcing companies to upgrade
to Microsoft Server 2003?

As far as the Redhat should be worried comment in the mentioned article,
why?  Redhat is in a different market than Microsoft is.  Microsoft has
no grounds to threaten Linux users with patent infringement lawsuits.
The purpose of patents is to increase public access to and fair use of
technology.  Attempting to use the patent system to create an empire is
an abuse of it and shows a lack of consideration.

For a while, I've been hoping that ReactOS will become more functional
for deskop use.  I think it would be better to prove to Microsoft and
the world that you don't need Windows, or any Windows compatible system,
to accomplish fantastic computing feats.  

Windows is not a good operating system.  Microsoft basically ignores the
Internet Engineering Task Force's every recommendation.  The registry
concept of Windows has become a monstrosity as various software vendors
and even Microsoft itself have abused it.  If the courts would get their
act together, Microsoft would be in trouble for threatening to sue Linux
users without grounds to do so.  

Isn't harassment against the law no matter how rich and powerful you
think you are?  Isn't it slanderous to lie about patent infringement
from a competitor when there isn't any infringement?  Does this strike
anyone, lying about patent infringement, as anticompetitive?

I think the response to this partnership is to generate more demand for
Linux.  If Microsoft is crazy enough to try and sue Linux users, I hope
people rise up and put Steve Ballmer in his place.  By rising up I'm
advocating: Microsoft software boycotts, helping people use alternative
software, and helping further the development of open source software
solutions.

Michael C. Robinson

On Sun, 5 Nov 2006, Winterbeast wrote:

>> I need it to sort the data based on the field "Number", which is also in
>> "Test_Table". I tried appending SORT ON "Number" FROM "Test_Table" but
>> OOo puked it up.

   Rightly so. Feed it garbage and it complains. There are two aggregating
commands, and the one you want is 'group by.' Try "select * from test_tickle
where field_name = 'ipa' group by 'number'". I don't know the specific SQL
dialect used by OO.o.

I echo Rich on Slackware but thats just a guttural response. It boils down
to a couple of things both of which you touched on.

A) Legality - I don't think any of us are lawyers? If you wanted to avoid
the lawsuits and IP issues associated with Linux there is also FreeBSD.

B) What are you going to use it for? From an ease of use standpoint I'd lean
towards Fedora or Ubuntu although I'm not partial to either since as
mentioned above I'm a slackware user :-) Or if you're really into getting
something that *should* be clean and a challenge you could always go linux
from scratch (http://www.linuxfromscratch.org/) has been one of the things
I've wanted to get around to doing myself. Think incredibly compact
webserver.

Let us know what you decide!

gives.

From chgenly at verizon.net  Sun Nov  5 20:58:27 2006
From: chgenly at verizon.net (Chris Genly)
Date: Sun, 05 Nov 2006 20:58:27 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] I say "Uncle"!
Message-ID: <454EC0F3.4050209@verizon.net>

I have just about given up on Linux.  I feel bad about it.  Linux has
many good things going for it.  I love the KDE destkop, I love the power
of the command line, and I love the networking power it empowers me
with.  I love that it is free in both senses of the word.  But I'm
getting tired of the missing things.  Things like device drivers that
fully support a device, video and audio codecs, and games. 

I don't want to support Microsoft,  a confirmed monopoly.  But in fact
every time I buy a machine it comes with windows anyway.   I support
them against my will.

In the wireless area I have never been able to get a laptop to work well
with wireless.  I can configure it to connect to a particular network,
but I was never able to get it to scan for available networks and then
configure for one of them.  I think the problem is my wireless driver is
not complete.   Under windows this just works.

In the codec area, I am tired of having to boot windows to listen to
certain audio and video feeds.   For example I like to listen to
zefrank.com occasionally.  But I haven't been able to get it to work on
linux.  In windows this just works.

And of course the problem we are all aware of with games is that
manufacturers write for windows and don't give a care for linux.

And finally, I am getting tired of all the tinkering I have to do to
keep things working.  I might be able to fix the codec problem with
enough research, but I just don't want to do that anymore.

I am a proponent of platform independent software.   I write in Java, I
use thunderbird and firefox.  I'll continue to support platform
independence when possible.

I want Gnu/Linux and FOSS to succeed.  I hope these problems are fixed
over time.   But for now I think I'm going to switch.  Who knows, after
a while I may be so irritated by Windows and Microsoft that I'll switch
back.

Chris

From ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com  Sun Nov  5 22:28:23 2006
From: ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com (Carlos Konstanski)
Date: Sun, 5 Nov 2006 23:28:23 -0700 (MST)
Subject: [PLUG] lisp problem: switching packages on the fly
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0611052243230.12285@sphinktoo.pippiandcarlos.com>

Been beating my head against the monitor on this lisp problem.  Maybe
someone can help.

The following snippet of lisp code is from my web server.  I have more
than one website running in the server, and the websites have many
shared resources.  For instance, the stylesheet is identical for all the
websites, except the specific values (colors, font names, etc.).  So
each website has its own skin-config list, whereas the stylesheet
generating function itself is shared by all websites.

Each website lives in its own package.  There's a :wrlug-site, a
:jewelry-site, and a :pippiandcarlos-site presently, with more to come.
Each of these sites has its own skin-config, therefore there is a
wrlug-site:skin-config, a jewelry-site:skin-config, and a
pippiandcarlos-site:skin-config.  But there is only one function
(stylesheet-body), which lives in a parent package called :araneida-site.
:araneida-site does not use any of the aforementioned packages.  Indeed,
there would be symbol conflicts aplenty if I attempted this, since each
webapp package has many of the same symbol names, of which skin-config
is just one.  The idea is to have as many shared resources as possible,
and to be able to use these resources without having to pass around a
lot of data and functions in argument lists to make them accessible to
the shared functions.

So when I get to the point in the execution of a page where I'm calling
(araneida-site:stylesheet-body), I need to direct this function to call
upon symbols from the correct package, corresponding to the webapp the
user is in when he sent a request that caused (araneida-site:stylesheet-body)
to be called.  Ideally I would like to switch the current package to
<webapp-package>, execute the code, and (if necessary) switch back to
:araneida-site.  This seems like the cleanest way to make a single body
of code work across a bunch of packages.

This is as far as I got.  The current package does indeed change.  I can
tell this because my REPL prompt changes to the new package name.  But a
condition is signaled: "The variable SKIN-CONFIG is unbound".  However,
if I type "skin-config" in the REPL after the package change, the value of
skin-config is found, and its contents displayed.

If I cannot switch packages on the fly inside a function, I would settle
for a macro that prepends the package name to a symbol, so I could write
something like (prepend-package skin-config), and end up with
jewelry-site:skin-config in its place, though it's less desirable because
I would have to alter many lines of code to do something that should be
possible with one line at the top.

Any ideas would be appreciated.

Here's a complete code listing for a clinical test case.  The expected
output would be a CSS body{} element, with colors and font names
substituted in place of the skin-config queries.  It should be called
like:

(in-package #:araneida-site)
(stylesheet-body "jewelry-site")



;; ====== ;;

(defpackage #:jewelry-site
   (:export #:skin-config)
   (:use #:cl))

(in-package #:jewelry-site)

(defparameter skin-config `(:color-canvas "#539083"
                             :color-background "white"
                             :color-dark "black"
                             :color-medium "#779193"
                             :color-light "#dddddd"
                             :color-white "white"
                             :color-alink "blue"
                             :color-vlink "maroon"
                             :color-error "red"
                             :color-highlight "yellow"
                             :font-family "verdana, tahoma, helvetica, arial, sans"
                             :font-size-default "14px"
                             :font-size-text "12px"
                             :font-size-tinytext "10px"
                             :border "white 0px solid")
   "A list of all style values for the webapp.")

;; ====== ;;

(defpackage #:araneida-site
   (:use #:cl))

(in-package #:araneida-site)

(defun stylesheet-body (webapp-package)
   "Outputs the body of the stylesheet."
   (let ((webapp-package-coerced-to-string (string-upcase (format nil "~a" webapp-package))))
     (setf *package* (find-package webapp-package-coerced-to-string))
     (use-package *package*)    ;; redundant?
     `(,(concatenate 'string
"body {
     background-color: " (getf skin-config :color-canvas) ";
     color: " (getf skin-config :color-dark) ";
     font-family: " (getf skin-config :font-family) ";
     font-size: " (getf skin-config :font-size-default) ";
     font-weight: normal;
     scrollbar-arrow-color: " (getf skin-config :color-medium) ";
     scrollbar-track-color: " (getf skin-config :color-medium) ";
     scrollbar-highlight-color: " (getf skin-config :color-medium) ";
     scrollbar-darkshadow-color: " (getf skin-config :color-medium) ";
     scrollbar-shadow-color: " (getf skin-config :color-medium) ";
     scrollbar-face-color: " (getf skin-config :color-white) ";
     scrollbar-3dlight-color: " (getf skin-config :color-medium) ";
}"))))

Carlos Konstanski

On Sun, 5 Nov 2006, drew wymore wrote:
> Or if you're really into getting something that *should* be clean and a 
> challenge you could always go linux from scratch 
> (http://www.linuxfromscratch.org/) has been one of the things I've 
> wanted to get around to doing myself.

I've built several systems "from scratch" (you've got to bootstrap it 
somehow, of course, so you're probably starting with a simple development 
Debian environment and then building a bootable system inside that which 
then becomes the primary system so you can delete the binary installation) 
and ran them for several years.

They were a bit of a hassle to maintain, but doing it certainly teaches 
you a lot about the system architecture and gives you respect for an 
elegant and well-ordered package management system.

> Think incredibly compact webserver.

Yeah, well, it turns out... not so much.

A bare Debian system with just the packages you'd like to have installed 
is way smaller than a "from scratch" system because you don't have any of 
the development utilities or libraries.  Also, they're faster and easier 
to build.

J.

      Jeme A Brelin

From gilmanhunt at comcast.net  Sun Nov  5 23:20:59 2006

Subject: [PLUG] SQL Syntax
In-Reply-To: <454E905B.4040405@verizon.net>
References: <20061105114624.1fd5c48c.johnxj@comcast.net>
	<454E905B.4040405@verizon.net>
Message-ID: <20061105232059.0fe42858@badger.had1.or.comcast.net.>

On Sun, 05 Nov 2006 17:31:07 -0800
Winterbeast <winter.beast at verizon.net> wrote:

> John Jason Jordan wrote:
> 
> >I just know there are people here who dream in SQL commands. My
> >knowledge of SQL is negligible. I need to change an SQL command that
> >reads a table in an OOo Base file and displays it in a control in a
> >Writer form document. The current syntax is SELECT DISTINCT "IPA"
> >FROM "Test_Table". I need it to sort the data based on the field
> >"Number", which is also in "Test_Table". I tried appending SORT ON
> >"Number" FROM "Test_Table" but OOo puked it up. I don't have time to
> >take a course on SQL commands (I actually tried reading a book on it
> >once and found it hopeless for me). The problem is that I need to
> >deal with SQL commands only once in a blue moon; not enough to be
> >worth my time to become an expert. Can someone tell me what is the
> >secret to getting the SELECT command to sort the data when it
> >displays it in the OOo form control?
> >_______________________________________________ PLUG mailing list
> >PLUG at lists.pdxlinux.org

Given the parameters you've supplied, it sounds like you need "order
by", as in "select distinct ipa from test_table order by number."
That'd be mysql and mssql syntax. I don't know specifically about
oobase syntax. 

"Group by" is a completely different beast; that's good for things like
"select count(*), author from books order by author"; it won't do the
ordering you're asking for.

Assuming you've copied the syntax right, you'll probably want double
quotes around "number" but not around "order by." In mysql-ese, you'd
be using backticks to delineate the column names.

I don't actually _dream_ in SQL, though.

-- 
Russ Gilman-Hunt
http://www.arghwebworks.com/
gilmanhunt at comcast.net

As I wrote just minutes ago, I ran LFS systems for years (back from maybe 
2000 to 2003 or so?).

They're not the tiny things you might think.  The development environment 
is kind of huge.  If you want to pare something down, you're better off 
building something inside a UML or chroot environment that is exactly what 
you need and then making an image of that and putting it on a new machine. 
No compilation required.

drew wymore wrote:
>> I've built several systems "from scratch" (you've got to bootstrap it
>> somehow, of course, so you're probably starting with a simple development
>> Debian environment and then building a bootable system inside that which
>> then becomes the primary system so you can delete the binary
>> installation)
>> and ran them for several years.
>>
>> They were a bit of a hassle to maintain, but doing it certainly teaches
>> you a lot about the system architecture and gives you respect for an
>> elegant and well-ordered package management system.
>>
>> > Think incredibly compact webserver.
>>
>> Yeah, well, it turns out... not so much.
>>
>> A bare Debian system with just the packages you'd like to have installed
>> is way smaller than a "from scratch" system because you don't have any of
>> the development utilities or libraries.  Also, they're faster and easier
>> to build.

Actually, you can probably get a LAMP stack, including a primitive GUI,
on a 128 MB stick using a compressed filesystem. Damn Small Linux was
born at 50 MB for just the kernel and desktop. I can't imagine needing
more than another 78 MB for Apache, MySQL and PHP. Now where your web
apps will store their data is another story ...

Another option for a small system would be a Gentoo "stage3" install. I
forget how big that is, but the whole toolset fits on a compressed 50 MB
business card CD. It is command-line only, though -- no GUI.

Also, there's LAMPPIX:

http://lamppix.tinowagner.com/en/mini/

From turner at glsuite.com  Mon Nov  6 08:08:38 2006
From: turner at glsuite.com (Mark A. Turner)
Date: Mon, 6 Nov 2006 08:08:38 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] SQL Syntax
In-Reply-To: <86d580q5gw.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
Message-ID: <602E70A3AE4B924788440D1F5D572CC779D40E@glsuite01.c2msnet.local>


 
> My SQL is quite rusty, but I am suspicious about being able to order
> results on a field that isn't being selected.  You might want to try
> adding the "Number" field to the SELECT list.

ORDER BY is based on the table your selecting from, not the data your
selecting.

So:
 SELECT v.Type from veggies v
 ORDER BY v.Price,v.Quantity

Would select all the data from the Type column and sort that based on
Price, then Quantity before returning the results. This is pretty much
common among all SQL servers.

-mark

On Sun, 05 Nov 2006 23:18:08 -0800
"M. Edward (Ed) Borasky" <znmeb at cesmail.net> dijo:

> John Jason Jordan wrote:
> > Problem: Can't embed fonts in a form control on OOo Writer document
> > when exporting from OOo to PDF. I need an alternative PDF creator.

> Have you tried Scribus? It's a bit more like PageMaker than Acrobat, but
> it might do a better job than Open Orifice (which, by the way, I detest!)
> 
> I have lots of PDF-making tools on my Gentoo box. Surely one of them
> will do what you want to do. Also, are you sure you have all the fonts
> you need totally installed?

I have, indeed, tried Scribus. I've used it off and on for little
things. The problem is that it is designed for desktop publishing, and
this project needs an office-type suite. To repeat the problem: I am
designing a form with drop-down buttons tied to a database for students
to select the correct answer from the contents of the field in the
database table. Adobe Reader 7.0 will allow edits of this sort in a PDF
file. The students won't be able to save a copy (although there are
workarounds), but they will at least be able to print it out for
themselves or to hand in to the professor. Scribus is a very nice app,
but it doesn't have controls that I can put on a form.

OOo has all the functionality I need, except that its export to PDF is
sort of broken. It is not embedding the font that I applied to the
controls. In fact, last night I moved my most recent PDF attempt to my
Windows desktop (where the font I used is not installed) and discovered
that OOo isn't embedding the font anywhere. It's just embedding a
pointer to it, and for the controls, not even that. Hence, when I open
the PDF on my Linux computer it displays the regular portions of the
text correctly (because the font is installed here), but for the
controls it substitutes some ugly thing that doesn't have all the IPA
characters I need. On my Windows desktop Adobe Reader substitutes the
ugly, useless font everywhere.

The controls do appear properly as a OOo document. So OOo is applying
the font correctly to the controls. It's just in the export that it's
broken. Since it appears correctly as an OOo form document, I thought
that a different PDF creation utility would be the next thing to try.
However, creating editable PDFs like this is cutting edge in the PDF
world. Adobe Reader 7.0 was the first reader that could display
editable PDFs like this. If I open my PDFs in Kpdf, Gpdf, Evince, or
anything else, the controls are just gray images -- no editing
capability. And that's a PDF that *is* editable in Adobe Reader 7.0.
The result is that I think there is no point in trying the toy PDF
creators, or anything which has had no development done on it for a
couple of years.

OOo is doing the job for me as far as the document creation goes
(although I spent the better part of a day figuring out how to create
forms with controls and how to set up the database in Base, and I've
still got a problem displaying the records in the controls in proper
sort order). It's the export to PDF function that is broken. I'm using
OOo 2.03 on my Ubuntu Dapper laptop, but I can't find the latest 2.04
in the repositories. I posted a query on the Ubuntu forums to see if
someone had figured out how to install 2.04, but no responses so far.
On the OOo website it has only an RPM for download. A couple of times
in the past I've tried to convert an RPM to a DEB with alien, but have
never been successful. It's a long shot, and there's no way to tell if
the problem has been fixed in 2.04 anyway -- at least scouring the OOo
forums has not turned up anything on point.

I'd just go buy Acrobat 7.0 or 8.0 (previous versions can't create
editable PDFs), but there's no way to get it to run on Linux, except
maybe with vmware or qemu. I don't really want to install a whole extra
OS on this computer. Adobe also has an online PDF creator but, of
course, it only supports Microsoft and Adobe products. However, it will
also create a PDF from a PostScript print file, and that is what I am
investigating next. I need to figure out how to install a driver that
will print to file instead of to a printer through the network or a
port or something. I gave up last night about 11:00 when my eyes
refused to focus any more. Now it's morning and I'm back to work on the
problem.

Thanks for the suggestions. I'm sure there's a way to do it on Linux.
It's just a question of finding the right tools.


From johnxj at comcast.net  Mon Nov  6 08:56:26 2006

On Mon, 6 Nov 2006 08:08:38 -0800
"Mark A. Turner" <turner at glsuite.com> dijo:

> > My SQL is quite rusty, but I am suspicious about being able to order
> > results on a field that isn't being selected.  You might want to try
> > adding the "Number" field to the SELECT list.
> 
> ORDER BY is based on the table your selecting from, not the data your
> selecting.
> 
> So:
>  SELECT v.Type from veggies v
>  ORDER BY v.Price,v.Quantity
> 
> Would select all the data from the Type column and sort that based on
> Price, then Quantity before returning the results. This is pretty much
> common among all SQL servers.

The first thing I did was to observe the syntax that OOo Base used to
select the data from the "IPA" table. It was

SELECT DISTINCT "IPA" FROM "Test_Table"

Observing the above, I decided to wing it in the hopes that I could get
it right. I appended "SORT ON" to the above:

SELECT DISTINCT "IPA" FROM "Test_Table" SORT ON "Number"

But OOo Base puked that up. Hey, I'm not a programmer. "SORT ON" is the
way I would say it. All the programmers I know love to tell me how
modern programming languages are easy because they're English-like.
Well, evidently, programming languages do not enjoy a vocabulary as
large as mine.

So I asked here and, after a couple people responded, I changed it to
"ORDER BY." That seemed to satisfy OOo Base. No error messages. But it
also didn't work. The records in the IPA field are displayed in the
control, but still in the strange random order as before. Since there
are 105 records,  students will have to scroll up and down to find the
correct answer, so having them in a logical order is important.

Later I discovered that if you select a control in the OOo form,
right-click on it and then on Form (instead of Control), it changes the
property window and you have a place where you can select the sort
order. This is a different box frrom the Select box, in fact, it is on
a different tab. It had a "..." button to the right, which popped up a
list of the fields in Test_Table. I selected the Number field, and
happily concluded that I had finally found the right button to get it
to work. I also deleted the ORDER BY from the entry in the Data tab.
Sadly, it still does not work. No error messages; it just doesn't work.
The records are still displayed in the control in the same strange
random order.

I also subscribe to a User e-list for OOo and I posted the problem
there. Unfortunately, I use my Hotpop account for that e-list, and
Hotpop has occasional bouts of constipation, followed by diarrhea. At
the moment it's in constipation mode, so even my own post has not
appeared in my inbox. I'm hoping that I will eventually get a response
there that will lead me to the solution.


From keithl at kl-ic.com  Mon Nov  6 09:01:00 2006
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Mon, 6 Nov 2006 09:01:00 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Games and Linux and Life
In-Reply-To: <454EC0F3.4050209@verizon.net>
References: <454EC0F3.4050209@verizon.net>
Message-ID: <20061106170100.GA26662@gate.kl-ic.com>

On Sun, Nov 05, 2006 at 08:58:27PM -0800, Chris Genly wrote:
...
> And of course the problem we are all aware of with games is that
> manufacturers write for windows and don't give a care for linux.
...

Games.  One of the reasons I run Linux is that I have a semi-
addictive personality, and games would suck up entirely too much
of my life that I would rather use productively.  There are just
too many positive things that I can do, and need doing, and not
enough hours to do them in.   So games get erased on my machines,
and if the urge becomes overpowering I actually firewall off some
game websites so I can resist temptation.

Most of you are younger than me, and grew up with computer and
video games, and perhaps some of you have spent thousands of hours
on them.  So how does the thrill of winning a video game compare
to completing a small program, or finding a bug, or building a
cabinet, or playing music with friends, or some other small task
with a defined result?  Does game playing scratch the same itch?
For me, game playing is almost self-destructive, it is the 
internal brat fighting against the outwardly successful adult.

The one gamelike addiction I permit myself is Sudoku puzzles out
of the paper, but even there it was more satisfying to write a
solver in Perl (which has solved every puzzle so far, though a
16x16 5 star from the Oregonian takes almost a minute to solve
by machine, and hours by hand).  Still, that is time taken away
from other things.

The reason there are so few games for Linux may be because Linux,
and creativity in general, are much more engaging games.  Perhaps
if we developed some game-like debugging tools, then the young
folk spending kilo-hours looking for monsters in mazes could be
looking for buffer overflows instead.

Keith

-- 
Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993
KLIC --- Keith Lofstrom Integrated Circuits --- "Your Ideas in Silicon"
Design Contracting in Bipolar and CMOS - Analog, Digital, and Scan ICs

From merlyn at stonehenge.com  Mon Nov  6 08:47:16 2006
From: merlyn at stonehenge.com (Randal L. Schwartz)
Date: 06 Nov 2006 08:47:16 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Re: SQL Syntax
References: <86d580q5gw.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
	<602E70A3AE4B924788440D1F5D572CC779D40E@glsuite01.c2msnet.local>
Message-ID: <86zmb4h697.fsf@blue.stonehenge.com>

>>>>> "Mark" == Mark A Turner <turner at glsuite.com> writes:

Mark> ORDER BY is based on the table your selecting from, not the data your
Mark> selecting.

I'm with Russell on this.  ORDER BY is looking at the result set,
not the original table.  If you don't select something, you can't
ORDER BY it.

As an indication of that, I often use "ORDER BY 2" to order by the second
column of the result rows.

At least in standard SQL.  We're not talking about the seriously dainbramaged
MySQL here.  (Hint: please stop using MySQL... PostgreSQL is far more standard
and useful and scaleable.)

At least PostgreSQL tells you that you can't order by something that you
haven't selected or computed.  MySQL breaks again by letting you ask for
something that you aren't getting, but not telling you about it.

From wcooley at nakedape.cc  Mon Nov  6 09:17:12 2006
From: wcooley at nakedape.cc (Wil Cooley)
Date: Mon, 06 Nov 2006 09:17:12 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Anyone good with LDAP?
In-Reply-To: <e2aeccd60611052109u5a9e9e51q7435a8cc168ea74f@mail.gmail.com>
References: <e2aeccd60611052109u5a9e9e51q7435a8cc168ea74f@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <1162833432.3719.10.camel@willow.odshp.com>

On Sun, 2006-11-05 at 21:09 -0800, drew wymore wrote:
> Evening All,
> I currently have a box setup using LDAP + NSS for user authentication which
> is working like a charm. However I've gotten to the point where I have
> enough users who want to change their password (darn users!). I used to use
> a web app called LDAP Manager (http://lam.sourceforge.net) but at this point
> its getting to be a chore to change user passwords for many reasons
> (security being the top issue). I've found many examples on the web of ways
> to write a stand-alone app using php/perl or some variant of and have
> limited success it getting them to work, rolling my own has not yielded
> anything workable at this point either. I've run into a problem essentially
> with the application not being able to bind as the user, it can bind _only_
> as the manager account. I'm loathe to allow users to change passwords while
> being logged in as the manager. My hand LDAP admin book doesn't show any
> ACL's which should preclude the user from auth'ing so I have no idea what
> gives.
> 
> Any suggestions?

Assuming you're talking about OpenLDAP, then you need this as part of
your ACLs:

access to attr=userPassword
    by self write
    by anonymous auth

Wil
-- 
Wil Cooley <wcooley at nakedape.cc>
http://nakedape.cc

> Later I discovered that if you select a control in the OOo form,
> right-click on it and then on Form (instead of Control), it changes
the
> property window and you have a place where you can select the sort
> order. This is a different box frrom the Select box, in fact, it is on
> a different tab. It had a "..." button to the right, which popped up a
> list of the fields in Test_Table. I selected the Number field, and
> happily concluded that I had finally found the right button to get it
> to work. I also deleted the ORDER BY from the entry in the Data tab.
> Sadly, it still does not work. No error messages; it just doesn't
work.
> The records are still displayed in the control in the same strange
> random order.

Well based on what you have said, I would chalk this one up as an issue
with OOo forms. With most development, even if your selecting data from
a source such as a DB and your sorting the returning data in SQL, you
cant be sure that the order will be maintained in the language/data
structure that storing it for future use. 

I have absolutely no experience with OOo Base so I'm afraid I cannot be
of much help there. But if OOo does keep the order of the data returned
from the DB then the ORDER BY clause is what you want, even if its not
working now it is the standard way or sorting results in SQL, remember
it.

I know this is going to sound like a dumb question, but I am going to
ask anyways. 

Have you googled around a little? 

Good Luck
-Mark

> ORDER BY it.

The only time the ORDER BY Clause is limited to the result set is when
your using a SELECT DISTINCT <COLUMN NAME>, other wise you have access
to any tables used in the query.

Erm, not so.

testdb=# select * from test_table\g
         name         |  id  
----------------------+------
 Wil Cooley           |    0
 Mark Turner          |  500
 Randal Schwartz      |  666
 Russell Senior       | 1000
(4 rows)

testdb=# select name from test_table order by id desc;
         name         
----------------------
 Russell Senior      
 Randal Schwartz     
 Mark Turner         
 Wil Cooley          
(4 rows)

testdb=# select name from test_table order by id asc;
         name         
----------------------
 Wil Cooley          
 Mark Turner         
 Randal Schwartz     
 Russell Senior      
(4 rows)

testdb=# select id from test_table order by name;
  id  
------
  500
  666
 1000
    0
(4 rows)


> As an indication of that, I often use "ORDER BY 2" to order by the second
> column of the result rows.

"SQL in a Nutshell" p146 says, "All implementations discussed here [SQL
Server, MySQL, Oracle & PostgreSQL] also allow the use of ordinal
positions in the /ORDER_BY/ clause."

> At least in standard SQL.  We're not talking about the seriously dainbramaged
> MySQL here.  (Hint: please stop using MySQL... PostgreSQL is far more standard
> and useful and scaleable.)
> 
> At least PostgreSQL tells you that you can't order by something that you
> haven't selected or computed.  MySQL breaks again by letting you ask for
> something that you aren't getting, but not telling you about it.

*whistles nonchalantly*

By the way, why is it that every time I upgrade PostgreSQL I have to
dump and restore my tables?

On Mon, 6 Nov 2006, Wil Cooley wrote:

> By the way, why is it that every time I upgrade PostgreSQL I have to dump
> and restore my tables?

Wil,

   A dump 'n' restore should be necessary only with a major upgrade. If
you're upgrading from 8.1.4 to 8.1.5, for example, you can do it without
disturbing the dust on the data. However, upgrading from 7.x to 8.x includes
disk storage format changes that require data to be dumped from the old
format and restored to the new format.

Rich

References: <20061105210432.aa07baa8.johnxj@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <20061106210039.GE28083@syrinxpc.com>

On Sun, Nov 05, 2006 at 09:04:32PM -0800, John Jason Jordan wrote:
> Does anyone know how to create a PostScript printer in CUPS that
> prints to file? I ask because the Adobe online service can take a .ps
> print file.

Check "print to file" when you print.  That generates a postscript file.
I do that a lot, and use ps2pdf to make a PDF out of it.

In fact, I generally "print to file" the receipt-pages from e-payments
and then convert those to PDF in bulk whenever they start to use too
much disk space.

Going the other way, note that pdftops and pdf2ps work rather
differently from each other.

On Sun, 5 Nov 2006, John Jason Jordan wrote:

> Problem: Can't embed fonts in a form control on OOo Writer document
> when exporting from OOo to PDF. I need an alternative PDF creator.

Are the fonts marked as "non-embedable"?  Some fonts have restrictions 
in the font file that prevents them from being embedded in documents. 
(For anything that pays attention to the flag.)

Either you need to find a font without that flag set or be a scofflaw and 
reset the flag yourself.

> Check "print to file" when you print.  That generates a postscript file.
> I do that a lot, and use ps2pdf to make a PDF out of it.

Ah! I had seen that box before and never used it. Much easier than
trying to create a print-to-file driver in CUPS. 

However, there is bad news. The printer I used to print to file is a
Laserjet 5SiMx (just like the one at Free Geek). It has genuine Adobe
PostScript Level 2. I printed a paper copy of the form on this printer
and it came out fine. So I uploaded the .ps file to Adobe's online
conversion utility. It worked great. (You get five free trials, so it
didn't cost me anything.) I downloaded the finished PDF, which Adobe
had cleverly set to open automatically in Adobe Reader. (It also
downloaded and opened a PDF announcing how I would enjoy a improved sex
life and become richer than Bill Gates, if only I would buy Acrobat.)

Ignoring the advertising PDF, I looked eagerly at the PDF of my file.
It looked perfect, except no controls. It was not an editable PDF file
at all. 

I repeated the process, except this time I printed to file while in
"design mode" in OOo Writer. Same results.

I e-mailed Adobe support, but I bet it's a lost cause. I noticed while
uploading the .ps file that I could choose the PDF version -- Acrobat
3.0, 4.0 or 5.0. No Acrobat 7.0 or 8.0. I think the ability to create
editable PDFs came in with Acrobat 7.0. Just a guess, but one of the
issues with editable PDFs is DRM stuff. I bet Adobe didn't want to make
editable PDFs available online.

Subject: [PLUG] Determine kernel release of non-running kernel?
In-Reply-To: <8fcf3b560611061604t289634e1ia9c29345c15c1ee4@mail.gmail.com>
References: <8fcf3b560611061604t289634e1ia9c29345c15c1ee4@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <2434.198.102.182.85.1162860604.squirrel@webmail.whiz.to>

> Anyone know how to determine the kernel release of a non-running kernel?
> Like 'uname -r' but point it at a kernel file?
>

Try this command:

   strings [kernel file] | head -20

For 2.4 and 2.6 kernel files to which I currently have access, the
name shows up somewhere in this output.

Terry



From rsteff at comcast.net  Mon Nov  6 16:05:09 2006
From: rsteff at comcast.net (Richard C. Steffens)
Date: Mon, 06 Nov 2006 17:05:09 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Error reading block xxxx
Message-ID: <454FCDB5.8050903@comcast.net>

We went away for a week, so I shut down all the hardware in the house.
Upon our return, most of it started back up. My old 200 MHz machine
running RH 7.0 reports a problem. After saying something to the effect
that the filesystem hadn't been checked in a very long time (this
machine ordinarily stays running) I got the following:

--------------------------------------------------------------------
Error reading block 257756 (Attempt to read block from filesystem
resulted in short read) while reading indirect blocks of inode 98117.
NEC40GB: UNEXPECTED INCONSISTENCY; RUN fsck MANUALLY (i.e., without -a
or -p options)
--------------------------------------------------------------------
Then I was given the option of entering root's password or <ctrl>d to do
a normal boot, again.

First I tried to get away with a normal boot again. Didn't work. One
nice thing is that the error repeated with the same message as the first
time. So, I followed the directions. I logged in as root and was given
the prompt:

(Repair filesystem) 1#:

I ran man fsck, less /etc/fstab, and then:

--------------------------------------------------------------------
(Repair filesystem) 1#:fsck LABEL=NEC40GB

Parallelizing fsck version 1.18 (11-Nov-1999)
e2fsck 1.18, 11-Nov-1999 for EXT2 FS 0.5b, 95/08/09
NEC40GB contains a file system with errors, check forced.
Pass 1: Checking inodes, blocks, and sizes
--------------------------------------------------------------------

That was over an hour ago, and the screen hasn't changed. I realize it's
a 40GB drive and only a 200MHz processor, but shouldn't I see something
to indicate progress?

I suspect that I could edit fstab to prevent the 40GB drive from being
mounted during boot, but what would I do after that?

Recommended reading on diagnosing and repairing damaged file systems
would be appreciated.

In case anyone's wondering why RH 7.0, that's the machine that has it's
sound card wired to the stereo in the living room. The last time I tried
upgrading to a later version of the OS, I ran into latency problems that
would not go away. I have since read on the mpg123 web site that they
have made improvements that might solve this problem. Meanwhile, I've
been happy to live with the old OS, since this machine sits inside the
hardware firewall with NAT, so should be invisible to the rest of the world.

-- 
Regards,

Dick Steffens
